<span id="freeTextContainer4055251457663442908">I am lucky to have received an ARC copy of Tiger's Quest. I was simply giddy when I got it in the mail. I even did a little happy dance. You see, I have become obsessed with the Tiger series all over again. (I actually read the first two books in the series when Colleen was self published) I just love these books. It is going to take a awhile to get them out of my system.<br/><br/>Tiger's Quest will be take you on an emotional roller coaster ride as Kelsey, Ren and Kishan's adventure continues to break th</span>
  <span id="freeText4055251457663442908" style="display:none">I am lucky to have received an ARC copy of Tiger's Quest. I was simply giddy when I got it in the mail. I even did a little happy dance. You see, I have become obsessed with the Tiger series all over again. (I actually read the first two books in the series when Colleen was self published) I just love these books. It is going to take a awhile to get them out of my system.<br /><br />Tiger's Quest will be take you on an emotional roller coaster ride as Kelsey, Ren and Kishan's adventure continues to break the second part of the curse. The book has two main parts: In the first part of the book, Kelsey is back in Oregon going to school. I like seeing how she copes with Ren back in India. The second part of the story details the adventures of Kelsey and Kishan as they are tested both individually and together. I know you all love Ren and I do too, but in this book we get to know Kishan a lot better. Though I am a true fan of Ren the white tiger, Kishan the black tiger has warmed his way into my heart as well.<br /><br />I really can't thank Colleen enough for sharing her Tigers with us. This book has everything. Trust me you will love it. I am hoping as the adventure continues and they break more of the curse both Ren and Kishan will have a happy ending. But we will have to wait and see as book three Tiger's Voyage comes out this Nov. 1st, 2011.<br /><br />This is a MUST have for your library. I just finished it and am going to read it again. I have already pre-ordered my hardback. I hope one day to meet Colleen and have her sign my books. So come to NC Colleen!!!!<br />You can pick up the book here:<br /><br /><a href="http://www.amazon.com/Tigers-Quest-Book-Curse/dp/140278404X/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;s=books&amp;qid=1304472832&amp;sr=1-1" rel="nofollow noopener">http://www.amazon.com/Tigers-Quest-Book-Curse/dp/140278404X/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;s=books&amp;qid=1304472832&amp;sr=1-1</a><br /><br /><br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1226700893" />
    <a title="Lia Angelidou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7348023-lia-angelidou"><img alt="Lia Angelidou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506709257p2/7348023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1226700893?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lia Angelidou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lia Angelidou" href="/user/show/7348023-lia-angelidou">Lia Angelidou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8220052-tiger-s-quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7348023-lia-angelidou?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7348023-lia-angelidou?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7348023-lia-angelidou?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7348023-lia-angelidou?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7348023-lia-angelidou?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7348023-lia-angelidou?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7348023-lia-angelidou?shelf=recommended-by-friends">recommended-by-friends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1226700893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13609751756818310656">[“One’s enemy is often the best teacher of tolerance.”]<br/><br/>Tiger’s quest has the right dose of adventure and romance a reader needs. And admit it, it’s a combination us hopeless romantic readers can’t resist!<br/><br/>Writing Style<br/><br/>I think Colleen Houck succeeded in wrtiting this book. There are many different types of scenes and I was satisfied with the way they were discribed. There were romantic scenes were we could easily relate with Kelsey because we were inside her head all the time. There were thoughts,</span>
  <span id="freeText13609751756818310656" style="display:none">[“One’s enemy is often the best teacher of tolerance.”]<br /><br />Tiger’s quest has the right dose of adventure and romance a reader needs. And admit it, it’s a combination us hopeless romantic readers can’t resist!<br /><br />Writing Style<br /><br />I think Colleen Houck succeeded in wrtiting this book. There are many different types of scenes and I was satisfied with the way they were discribed. There were romantic scenes were we could easily relate with Kelsey because we were inside her head all the time. There were thoughts, feelings and great transition to dialogue. I also find amazing that even though it was a first person POV, the rest of the characters were described that way that the readers could also catch a glimpse of their feelings.<br /><br />There were action scenes, detailed enough but yet not tiring and that’s important because I can’t stand too much information. I mean yeah ok it’s good to know the surroundings of the characters but get to the point cause I don’t really care about the rest. I could easily picture what was happening in my mind and it was like I was experiencing the adventure with Kelsey.<br /><br />Last but not least there were descriptions about scenery and India and small villages and I loved the way they were portraited. I feel like I have to visit India after reading the book.<br /><br />Plot/World Building<br /><br />I think the first third of the book was absolutely unessacery drama. There was no point in writing it at all. Kelsey was in love with Ren and Ren was in love with Kelsey, the end. The book would be awesome if it wasn’t for the first (tiring) third. I felt like I was reading a different book at first and then transformed back into Tiger’s Quest. The pace was so slow at first and I was struggling to keep reading. At the end I got the adventure I was looking for.<br /><br />Because of my lack of knowledge about Indian History and world’s history in general, I can’t really tell if any of these stories and information is real. My guess is that they’re based in history and in facts and that makes the author well informed. It’s good that she studied and researched about what to write and how to connect her story with facts or to come up with new facts.<br /><br />I am not even sure If I make sense but I love it when the world that the author builds has no flaws and when I want to know more about it.<br /><br /><br />Characters<br /><br />I want to make it clear that I don’t like Kelsey. She is one of the most annoying character’s I’ve ever read about and the minus two stars in my rating is because of her.<br /><br />She is the biggest drama queen ever, she is immature and even though she claims to be loyal, I think she’s not. She left the man she loved because she thought he was too good for her and that he would break her heart. Let me quote for you~<br /><br />[“Why did you leave Ren?”<br />….<br />“First of all, he is gorgeous, and I am… not. He is also very wealthy. In fact, he comes from royalty. He is from a different culture and background, and he hasn’t dated much and-“]<br /><br />Do you people realize as well how stupid this sounds? Am I the only one? Are these reasons to leave the person you care about the most? Apparently, she is too insecure and has trust issues.She doesn’t really deserve a man like Ren. Most people feel insecure but that doesn’t mean that they should just give up. Following that logic, I shouldn’t leave my house because I am always afraid of being hurt and I should break up with my boyfriend because I am afraid of loosing him. Are you for real?<br /><br />And then there’s Kishan. If she loved Ren she wouldn’t have allowed anything to happen between them. That’s cheating and I do not approve. If someone tried to kiss me I would have slapped him and pushed him away on the spot because I know I love my boyfriend. Kelsey might love Ren, (I don’t really think so) but she’s looking for trouble.<br /><br />So, I really don’t like Kelsey and her way of thinking and acting.<br /><br />Ren is one of the most well written characters. Charming and sweet and he feels like royal. He can act his real age and he is so mature and gentle that I got chills everytime I was reading about him. He is sincere and his love is touching and deep and inspiring. He could be fair and he knew the right thing to say. if it wasn’t for Kishan I would have found my new book boyfriend.<br /><br />Mentioning Kishan… he is my favorite! He is such a tragic character and he is so intruiging. It’s not his bad boy side that made me feel so many things about him but his kind nature. Yes, he made mistakes and yes he was jealous of his brother but I find his regret to be genuine and pure and real. Kishan seems more realistic because he has flaws in addition to Ren who’s the perfect prince. Kishan needs love and it’s tragic that all the girls he’s loved belonged to his brother. It’s not Kishan’s fault that he always comes second. He is living with the guilt and he is blaming himself and even though I understand, I wish he could get over of what he did. He deserves a great well written heroine and definitelly not Kelsey.<br /><br />Overall<br /><br />I really liked the book a lot and I’ve already started reading the next one. If it wasn’t for Kelsey, the book would have been in my top 5 favorites. Sadly I can’t get over the fact that she is annoying and that she caused all this trouble. It is true that if she wasn’t like that, the story wouldn’t turn out the same but I would have preferred a more important reason for her to leave Ren. Anyway… 3 stars for this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13609751756818310656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_257512976" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257512976" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257512976?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=needed-more-editor">needed-more-editor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=needless-fucking-drama">needless-fucking-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=pacing-pacing-pacing">pacing-pacing-pacing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=actually-decent-to-my-shock">actually-decent-to-my-shock</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=author-to-return-to">author-to-return-to</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=you-need-pale-romance">you-need-pale-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257512976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12100901185840165578">Edit: 9/27/2014 Retroactively reducing my ratings for these books because when I first read them I did <i>not</i> notice the racism/cultural appropriation.<br/><br/>(I thought I'd take a leaf out of Jillian's book and load up with tags. I love the way her shelves are basically a miniature review before you even reach the text.)<br/><br/><br/><br/>Okay, Colleen Houck, you win. I am actually glad I read this book. There, I admit it. After the torturous struggle that was the first one, I persevered into this because I already owned it</span>
  <span id="freeText12100901185840165578" style="display:none">Edit: 9/27/2014 Retroactively reducing my ratings for these books because when I first read them I did <i>not</i> notice the racism/cultural appropriation.<br /><br />(I thought I'd take a leaf out of Jillian's book and load up with tags. I love the way her shelves are basically a miniature review before you even reach the text.)<br /><br /><br /><br />Okay, Colleen Houck, you win. I am actually glad I read this book. There, I admit it. After the torturous struggle that was the first one, I persevered into this because I already owned it and to my surprise, <i>I enjoyed myself</i>. I still won't read the third because I've heard the drama gets even worse and really, my delicate system cannot handle that shit. But props, Ms. Houck. You've won me over. When you start your next series, I will be waiting, because I think you actually have what it takes to be a good writer. I'm not sure you are one yet, but you can be. Keep working.<br /><br /><br />There are a lot of things here that I liked. The pacing is still kind of shit, but at least it's slightly improved. The writing is technically a <b>lot</b> more readable. In Tiger's Curse I would occasionally hit pages so bad that I could not finish them and had to set the book aside for the day. There were none of them here. Oh, and Kelsey is actually turning into kind of a badass, which was a pleasant surprise. No more of this given-a-divine-weapon-but-it's-really-for-the-guy nonsense. She is blowing shit up and shooting down giant metal birds and yeah, that was FUN. As for Ren and Kishan - their rivalry and all the mushy bullshit with Ren was annoying as hell and gave me major MAJOR Twilight flashbacks, but Kishan's development was about 90% good here and I like him considerably more now than I did before when he was just kind of a creeper.<br /><br />Now, bad things: needless drama. Strange pacing (chapters spent on Kelsey juggling three boyfriends because... because I have no fucking idea why she didn't just dump at least one of them who she was obviously not interested in - but then the whole central event of the big quest goes by in one chapter despite it consisting of four separate 'tests'). 10% sloppy Kishan characterization, in the bit where all his guilt about his past is basically erased by magical ravens who grant him the understanding he needed to forgive himself. Kelsey, despite blowing shit up all the time, still not being able to stand up to people and just speak her mind (though credit where credit is due - she may grow into this over time and it could be part of an arc). Kelsey-without-Ren sounding so much like New-Moon-Bella that I could honestly see Bella saying and thinking and doing the same things, and that is <b>not</b> a compliment. The use of the phrase 'alligator tears' - that means fake, Ms. Houck, not large. Absurd glorification of Ren's appearance. Unnecessary and sloppy 'look at me I did my research' infodumps that have nothing to do with the story. Kishan continually kissing Kelsey when she can't resist him and generally being an ass way too often until he finally grows up a bit more at the end. The villain, Lokesh ("Lokesh had the conniving persona of Emperor Palpatine mixed with the sadistic cruelty of Hannibal Lecter. He craved power at any price, like Lord Voldemort, and he displayed the pitiless brutality of Ming the Merciless who, like him, had killed his own daughter." Are you KIDDING me? Does it get more over the top?). The way the climactic rescue scene was confusing and hard to follow and explained afterwards for no good reason. The descriptions of obscene wealth in a country plagued by poverty.<br /><br />Looking at that, it seems like the bad far outweighs the good, but here's the thing: the bad were mostly small things, things I have faith that Houck can improve in as an author. Now, while I will not be continuing with this series (Jillian gave the third book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137753192" rel="nofollow noopener">two stars</a> and it was her glowing review of the first that convinced me to make them a priority in the first place) I'm content with having read it to this point. Net gain, I think.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12100901185840165578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_855564759" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/855564759" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/855564759?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer855564759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9842924541127851329">How about no stars? Is that a legitimate option. This one is pretty much horrible. I didn't really expect much for it. I'm doing it for my yearly I force myself to read an awful series just to see how much I can test my sanity challenge. That and I like to dissect these horrible books so that I have an idea what I'm getting into. To see full review click on one of the following links:<br/><br/><a href='http://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2014/02/17/the-first-twenty-pages-alone-will-put-you-in-a-coma/' rel='nofollow noopener'>My blog</a><br/><br/><a href='http://HowdyYAL.booklikes.com/post/792819/you-could-blow-your-liver-with-the-first-twenty-pages' rel='nofollow noopener'>Booklikes</a></span>
  <span id="freeText9842924541127851329" style="display:none">How about no stars? Is that a legitimate option. This one is pretty much horrible. I didn't really expect much for it. I'm doing it for my yearly I force myself to read an awful series just to see how much I can test my sanity challenge. That and I like to dissect these horrible books so that I have an idea what I'm getting into. <div id="review_319204253" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/319204253" />
    <a title="is mee... kissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2565113-is-mee-kissa"><img alt="is mee... kissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345116473p2/2565113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/319204253?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="is mee... kissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="is mee... kissa" href="/user/show/2565113-is-mee-kissa">is mee... kissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319204253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12614300533548716752">2.5<br/>okay, my little bouts of annoyance with Kelsey has reached the stage of constant annoyance. to make matters worse, said annoyance has unconsciously made me pinpoint all mistakes in the author's writing that otherwise, i would not have noticed. so now, i'm annoyed at Kelsey, and mildly annoyed with everyone else too!<p><b>The Hero</b><br/>she does a little bit of work and all the credit goes to her. what the hell does she do?! she tags along with the <i>real</i> heros, does small thing to help, and then returns whe</p></span>
  <span id="freeText12614300533548716752" style="display:none">2.5<br />okay, my little bouts of annoyance with Kelsey has reached the stage of constant annoyance. to make matters worse, said annoyance has unconsciously made me pinpoint all mistakes in the author's writing that otherwise, i would not have noticed. so now, i'm annoyed at Kelsey, and mildly annoyed with everyone else too!<p><b>The Hero</b><br />she does a little bit of work and all the credit goes to her. what the hell does she do?! she tags along with the <i>real</i> heros, does small thing to help, and then returns where everyone is like "we couldn't have done it without you!". undue credit gets on my nerves <i>horribly</i>! and the worst part is, the heros <i>actually</i> believe she's the one that is the hero. again, what the hell does she do besides answer the occasional question and act as assistant to the hero? although I'll admit she did step it up in the end - thankfully! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[but even when all she did was ask Mr. Kadam for help about the Himalayas. She goes back to India and he's all like, "if it wasn't for you, I would have never figured out the riddle was about the Himalayas." sure, that's true, but does he have to say it in such a way that she's the heroine of such a small task because she asked him a question that incidentally related to what he was searching for? it was an <i>accident</i>! stop treating her like a goddess! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></p><p><b>Contradictions</b><br />that girl is <i>always</i> contradicting herself! sure, a few contradictions i can handle, but it's happening too much! my favourite ones so far are about Kishan. you know, like the "i love Ren, I can't be with you." to the "even though there's a lot of space on the floor, i'll move to the side a little so that you can come sleep directly next to me." it's like she's <i>inviting</i> him to love her more (who the hell knows why he does) so that he can: A. get his heart broken, or B. get his heart broken after experiencing great hope that he will actually have a chance with her. How much can she <i>really</i> love Ren if she's offering his brother, who she <i>knows</i> likes her a lot more than a sister, to sleep next to her? mean! and she's so insensitive about the Kishan-Ren issue too. I feel sorry for Kishan having to be exposed to her like that for so long.</p><p>
  <b>Boys</b>
  <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />How is it, that a girl that hasn't had her first kiss, let alone a miniscule of experience with boys, suddenly get the attention of so many when there hasn't been any change except for the fact that she fell in love and is in depression mode? Damn it annoys me when that happens. Sure, I get having one or two or even three interests, but come on, <i>five</i> interests! one of which is legitimate, the second of which is also legitimate, but where the hell did the other three come from? they spontaneously burst out of nowhere! who all of a sudden has three guys drooling after them within a week, when it has never before happened in their life, and there was no change in said person except for a case of depression? honestly. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</p><p><b>The Chosen One</b><br />Plus, she seems to know so many things about what she's practically never heard of before. Right, i get that she's some 'Chosen One' and it comes naturally to her, but would it kill the author to add a little struggling here and there? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Even with the whole lightening power. I can deal with her suddenly being able to shoot lightening from her fingertips, what I can't deal with is that it comes naturally to her too. Matters of the mind, sure, but physical manifestations of her Chosen-ness? no, just no. I do not like it that she can just think about it manifesting in some way and then it happens exactly like she wants it. Sure she's powerful, but where's the difficulty to control such power? Or how about the inability to bring up the power again when she's not worried her boy toy is going to die? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></p><br /><br />and lastly, I've just figured out who Kelsey reminds me of.<br />*drumroll* none other than Bella Swan. *shudder*<br /><br />my favouite part was the epilogue. okay, that sounds bad - i don't mean that i was happy it was over, i mean I got a break from Kelsey's stupidity and actually saw her express some serious emotion. although what happened with Ren was predictable due to constant references throughout the Kelsey-Kishan quest, I liked that it allowed me to see Kelsey <i>sincerely</i> for once.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12614300533548716752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_185223906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185223906" />
    <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole"><img alt="Duchess Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499265843p2/2204947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185223906?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duchess Nicole" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole">Duchess Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of epic fantasy, young adult or adult romance readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-ya">genre-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-paranormal-shifters">genre-paranormal-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=e-pcs">e-pcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=favorites-of-all-time">favorites-of-all-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185223906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10072878740444866791">I am officially BLOWN AWAY. This is shaping up to be one of my all time favorite YA series. My heart is just racing right now and my thoughts are so jumbled up, I can't seem to get my mind wrapped around what just happened. That was without a doubt one of the best cliffhanger endings that I've ever read (though I can only safely say that because I have the next book waiting to be read), the best love triangle I've ever read, and a wonderful, emotional journey of a modern fantasy.<br/><br/>Kelsey has left </span>
  <span id="freeText10072878740444866791" style="display:none">I am officially BLOWN AWAY. This is shaping up to be one of my all time favorite YA series. My heart is just racing right now and my thoughts are so jumbled up, I can't seem to get my mind wrapped around what just happened. That was without a doubt one of the best cliffhanger endings that I've ever read (though I can only safely say that because I have the next book waiting to be read), the best love triangle I've ever read, and a wonderful, emotional journey of a modern fantasy.<br /><br />Kelsey has left India and Ren and returned to the states to begin her college life. She firmly believes that had this handsome Indian prince not been forced into their relationship, he would never have chosen her to be with. She believes that he needs to experience his new life in the modern world unfettered by their relationship. She, in turn, forces herself to take the plunge and begins what she thinks of as a normal college girl's life. <br /><br />Needless to say, this is not exactly what occurs. One thing leads to another, and dating and school take a backseat to the two Indian tigers that she can't seem to shake. Once again, Kelsey heads to India to try to break the second part of the curse, and to free Ren and Keishan.<br /><br />To say that this book took me places unexpectedly is a vast understatement. The author is fantastic in that she makes me comfortable with Kelsey's normal life and then throws the story in a direction that I never saw coming. Once they get to India and I once again feel like I'm good with THIS direction for the story, she does a one eighty and changes EVERYTHING that I thought I knew about this series!!! THIS OH, MY GOSH moment came out of nowhere and literally made me have to stop reading to process my emotions, to CHECK myself before I started bawling uncontrollably. I am just floored. Confused, and angry and sad and so freaking unrealistically excited about these books! <br /><br />The imagery that the author shoves into my head is outstanding. I expect from a fantasy author to be swept away to another world, to see things that don't exist anywhere but the minds of whimsy and dreams. That's the amazing thing about fantasy...anything goes. NOTHING is impossible! Somehow, Ms. Houck has taken a modern love story and made it fantastical, bouncing around between the world of today and the places that could exist only in this book series. <br /><br />The age level is appropriate for anyone who is able to read this extensive of a series. And I don't say this to turn away my devout romance reader friends, because the story is so magical, the love so pure and passionate between Kelsey and...well, AND... that I don't notice a lack of smexy. This is the type of book that makes me rethink my former opinion of the necessity of heavy romance. The talent of this author is so vast, her characters so complex and well developed, that she doesn't need to add those pesky attention grabbing scenes, hoping to target a larger reading audience. <br /><br />To touch on the love triangle...I must admit I'm a lover of the trope. I like the idea of being so wonderfully irresistible to TWO men that the decision to choose between them is just impossible. I know not everyone feels this way. (Buncha crazies!) But funny enough, this is just one MORE thing that is very well done here. It's weird how the triangle is almost necessary. I already know who will be chosen...it's nearly obvious at this point. But neither guy is more deserving, neither is the better choice. It's all about gut feeling and the magic of love...the importance of following your heart without losing it. <br /><br />If you have this series on you mountainous "to be read" shelf like I did, I can't encourage you enough to take the plunge. First book has some world building, but was still a four star read for me. This book, however, deserves the elusive, nonexistent sixth star. I feel comfortable saying that I like this book better than Mortal Instruments, better than Twilight, better than the many, many adult series that I've read. If I'm this excited now, on book two, I can't even imagine how I'm going to feel reading the next three books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10072878740444866791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_190748606" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190748606" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5882067-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327863504p2/5882067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190748606?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/5882067-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5882067-jen?shelf=best-of-the-best">best-of-the-best</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190748606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17703067953947261228">Tiger's Quest is arguably better than Tiger's Curse. In Colleen's second novel we dive right into the action. We learn about the turmoil and anguish that Kelsey has been going through ever since she left India, and ultimately Ren, at the end of Tiger's Curse. It was heartbreaking to read about her decision to start dating other men, but I admired her determination to try and move on. I for one would NEVER be able to do that if I had someone like Ren. Although her decision to leave Ren was hard t</span>
  <span id="freeText17703067953947261228" style="display:none">Tiger's Quest is arguably better than Tiger's Curse. In Colleen's second novel we dive right into the action. We learn about the turmoil and anguish that Kelsey has been going through ever since she left India, and ultimately Ren, at the end of Tiger's Curse. It was heartbreaking to read about her decision to start dating other men, but I admired her determination to try and move on. I for one would NEVER be able to do that if I had someone like Ren. Although her decision to leave Ren was hard to grasp, in TQ we learn more about why she chose to do it and I found myself agreeing with her reasons. <br /><br />In chapter five of TQ we learn that Ren has traveled to the U.S. to fight for Kelsey. During the following chapters we dive more into Ren's character and oh my goodness is he incredible. Kelsey is the center of his universe and he isn't afraid to express it. Ren's affection for Kelsey can be described with this one quote, "You know you are in love when you see the world in her eyes and her eyes everywhere in the world." Once again I bow down at Colleen's feet for taking her time with Ren and Kelsey's relationship. She allows the characters to grow and become stronger. Ren and Kelsey are devoted to each other and it is believable. <br /><br />Unfortunately, the course of true love never did run smooth. In order to protect Kelsey's life he selflessly allows himself to be captured by Lokesh's men so she may escape. Insert Kishan...Throughout the rest of the novel it is now up to Kelsey and Kishan to complete the next step of the journey and then save Ren's life. During this time the relationship between Kelsey and Kishan grows as well as the undeniable attraction Kishan has for kelsey. Holy rusted metal Batman, I see a love-triangle coming on!<br /><br />When the light bulbs in my head started flicking on and I recognized the path this novel was taking I became very scared and let me tell you why - I HATE LOVE-TRIANGLES! Ever since New Moon was released there has been nothing but love-triangles in every single YA romance novel I have ever read and I am disgusted by it. Not only is it completely overdone it is done wrong. I cannot stand how the heroine of a novel falls for the hero and expresses her undying love, how there is no one in her life but him. Then love interest #2 comes waltzing in and every word of devotion our heroine said to our hero goes flying out the friggn' window. Our heroine now is spending all her time thinking, fantasizing, dreaming, kissing, flirting and socializing with the cruel jerk that is love interest #2. All the while she's contemplating on how she still loves our hero but continues to spend time with the other guy. Then, of course, the heroine ALWAYS ends up with the hero in the end. Ya, I didn't see that coming miles away at all! <br /><br />I hate love-triangles because I always end up hating love interest #2 and I end up hating the heroine for falling for him. It is painful for me to read such novels because I can never connect with the heroine. I'm being torn in two because I always hate love interest #2 but the author is drilling me with reasons why I should like him. This, to me, is the number one reason why Colleen is different from others. She has accomplished what 99.9% of authors cannot do - she has made me fall in love with love interest #2. <br /><br />Kishan is such a wonderful person. When Kishan is introduced in Tiger's Curse he is a bit hot-headed, egotistical, and arrogant. In Tiger's Quest the layers of the onion are peeled away and we see the real Kishan. The real Kishan is noble, honorable, considerate, respectful, loving, caring, and a fighter. Right off the bat when Kishan starts to have feelings for Kelsey he hates himself for it. We see a man who is still painfully bearing the weight of the sin he committed over 300 years earlier and he does not want to commit that same sin again. To respect Kelsey and Ren he stays away from Kelsey and allows Ren to be with her. Unfortunately, due to unforeseeable circumstances Kishan and Kelsey are forced to travel on this journey together and it is hard for Kishan to keep his feelings under control. Although Kishan occasionally loses control and shows a little too much affection toward Kelsey the reader still understands that Kishan would do anything to not feel the way he does. <br /><br />Another reason why Colleen is so wonderful at writing love-triangles is she is true to her characters. She doesn't write about a heroine who is deeply in love with a hero and than stabs him in the back by falling for someone else. Kelsey is 100% devoted to Ren and when Kishan advances on her she fights back. Even though Kelsey isn't perfect and starts to enjoy her time with Kishan a little too much (who wouldn't!) she doesn't act on those feelings and still wholeheartedly chooses Ren. I love Kishan and do genuinely want him to be happy. I hope he finds his happily ever after, just like Kelsey and Ren have. <br /><br />Tiger's Quest is an emotional roller coaster ride. The characters are all so wonderful and you care about each and every one of them. The adventure is thrilling, suspenseful, exciting, and fun. Although you may find your eyes watering a bit much you trust that Colleen knows what she is doing and everything will work out in the end. Tiger's Quest is the perfect continuation to a wonderful series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17703067953947261228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fRTibq0GUSEF9gHss7IqOEo+P2obe1XtPuHwLACoq9HC4N0kjBTLxQwxQwLo+J0AlW6KmCuhMD1B7lkfuv/zzA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

Formerly a student at the University of Arizona, she worked as a nationally certified American Sign Language interpreter for seventeen years before switching careers to become an author. Colleen lives in Salem, Oregon, with her husband and a huge as</span>
  <span id="freeText9504258412037059675" style="display:none">New York Times Bestselling Author Colleen Houck is a lifelong reader whose literary interests include action, adventure, science fiction, and romance. Formerly a student at the University of Arizona, she worked as a nationally certified American Sign Language interpreter for seventeen years before switching careers to become an author. Colleen lives in Salem, Oregon, with her husband and a huge assortment of plush tigers. Follow her by signing up for her <a href="http://eepurl.com/UlplP" rel="nofollow noopener">e-newsletter</a>!</span>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I decided to find you, throw myself at your feet, and beg you to have mercy on me. Honestly, I’ll accept whatever you choose, Kelsey. Just don’t ask me to live apart from you again. Because...I can’t.&rdquo;</span>

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;There are many different types of kisses. There’s a passionate kiss of farewell—like the kind Rhett gave Scarlett when he went off to war. The kiss of I-can’t-really-be-with-you-but-I-want-to-be—like with Superman and Lois Lane. There’s the first kiss—one that is gentle and hesitant, warm and vulnerable. And then there’s the kiss of possession—which was how Ren kissed me now. <br />It went beyond passion, beyond desire. His kiss was full of longing, need, and love, like all those other kisses. But, it was also filled with promises and pledges, some of which seemed sweet and tender while others seemed dangerous and exciting. He was taking me over. Staking a claim. <br />He seized me as boldly as the tiger captured his prey. There was no escape. And I didn’t want to. I would have happily died in his clutches. I was his. And he made sure I knew it. My heart burst with a thousand beautiful blooms, all tiger lilies. And I knew with a certainty more powerful than anything I’d ever felt before that we belonged together. &rdquo;</span>
